b_divsec"><li data-priority=""><div><span title="In general, we use hi there in spoken English. It is informal and usually used in a positive, upbeat tone. It is not rude but if you want to be polite you can learn more about polite and formal greetings here. You should definitely avoid hi there in emails but it can be quite common in text messages(a more informal medium). Hi there is a friendly way to greet someone and acts as a way to show that you are open to a conversation. It is not necessarily polite but people respond well to hi there as informal English becomes more popular.">In general, we use<strong> hi there</strong> in spoken English. or “hi there” is one of many examples of emphasis. The greeting of “hello” or “hi” stands perfectly fine on its own, but in combination with “there” it becomes more emphatic. The “there” not only identifies the person being addressed more acutely, but it also reinforces the acknowledgment of that person.</div><div class="rwrl_cred rwrl_f"><div class="qna_algo"><div between Hi and Hey?</div><span class="b_expansion_chevron b_chevron_up"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 13 24" height="16" width="10"><path class="sv_ch" info about this page right now" id="wire7"><div class="df_alsocon b_primtxt" data-tag="RelatedQnA.ItemDetails"><div><div class="rwrl rwrl_small rwrl_padref">Hi and hey are two distinct expressions, the first is what might as well be called hi whilst the second is utilized to snatch some individual's consideration as in "Hey, what's that unidentified flying object?", "Hey, did you see a week ago's scene of ...?"; "Hey man, how you're doing?" and "Hey man, how's it going?"</div><div class="rwrl_cred rwrl_f"><div class="qna_algo"><div class="b_algo"><p><a
